  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c443d805-735a-4a81-96f1-55be831793c4'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

    };

<span id="freeTextContainer16795208688055521474">Based on an original new story by J.K. Rowling, Jack Thorne and John Tiffany, a new play by Jack Thorne, <i>Harry Potter and the Cursed Child</i> is the eighth story in the Harry Potter series and the first official Harry Potter story to be presented on stage. The play will receive its world premiere in London’s West End on July 30, 2016.<br/><br/>It was always difficult being Harry Potter</span>
  <span id="freeText16795208688055521474" style="display:none">Based on an original new story by J.K. Rowling, Jack Thorne and John Tiffany, a new play by Jack Thorne, <i>Harry Potter and the Cursed Child</i> is the eighth story in the Harry Potter series and the first official Harry Potter story to be presented on stage. The play will receive its world premiere in London’s West End on July 30, 2016.<br /><br />It was always difficult being Harry Potter and it isn’t much easier now that he is an overworked employee of the Ministry of Magic, a husband and father of three school-age children.<br /><br />While Harry grapples with a past that refuses to stay where it belongs, his youngest son Albus must struggle with the weight of a family legacy he never wanted. As past and present fuse ominously, both father and son learn the uncomfortable truth: sometimes, darkness comes from unexpected places.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes and no. Yes, this book is canon; it's the script for a play that JK Rowling approved, BUT JK Rowling did NOT write this. It is based on her charac<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes and no. Yes, this book is canon; it's the script for a play that JK Rowling approved, BUT JK Rowling did NOT write this. It is based on her characters and a "story" of hers, but other authors wrote the script.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1571798517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1571798517" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1571798517?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=plays">plays</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1571798517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14644597201653711675"><br/>3 1/2 stars. I completely get why many HP fans will be disappointed with this, but I have to admit: <b>I really enjoyed it</b>. I'd love to see this story play out on stage.<br/><br/>So yeah, I understand the sad feelings. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29056083.Harry_Potter_and_the_Cursed_Child__Harry_Potter___8_' title='Harry Potter and the Cursed Child (Harry Potter, #8) by J.K. Rowling' rel='nofollow noopener'>Harry Potter and the Cursed Child</a> has a completely different vibe. Aside from being a play, it's also a more mature, character-driven, less magical story. It does not feel like an eighth Harry Potter book at all; there's a real disconnect between this play and the other seven novels. And you k</span>
  <span id="freeText14644597201653711675" style="display:none"><br />3 1/2 stars. I completely get why many HP fans will be disappointed with this, but I have to admit: <b>I really enjoyed it</b>. I'd love to see this story play out on stage.<br /><br />So yeah, I understand the sad feelings. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29056083.Harry_Potter_and_the_Cursed_Child__Harry_Potter___8_" title="Harry Potter and the Cursed Child (Harry Potter, #8) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter and the Cursed Child</a> has a completely different vibe. Aside from being a play, it's also a more mature, character-driven, less magical story. It does not feel like an eighth Harry Potter book at all; there's a real disconnect between this play and the other seven novels. And you know what? I'm so glad. <br /><br />I guess it's just what you're hoping for. To be honest, <b>I never wanted another Harry Potter book</b>. The thought of extending a series I loved so much actually made me NOT want to read this. I got to the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/136251.Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows__Harry_Potter___7_" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows (Harry Potter, #7) by J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</a> and thought it was magical perfection - the story had completed its arc in full and I put it aside feeling a slight melancholy, but a whole lot of satisfaction. I didn't want more.<br /><br />However, if you went crazy needing more from the HP series, you'll probably be disappointed by this. If you feel there's a gap where something HP is missing, then I don't think this will fill it. Separate the two in your mind, and you have a better chance of liking it. Because this is something different - and I'm happy about it.<br /><br />First, of course, <b>it's a play</b>. Right away it's going to be something unlike what we've seen before. I don't usually love to read plays, especially modern ones, but this one is very readable because the <b>dialogue is wonderful</b>. I don't know why people are saying "it's so obvious JKR didn't write most of this" because I think her style is all over it - the very fact that this play (which is meant to be viewed on stage) can be just as easily read like a book tells me JKR had a lot of input.<br /><br />Also, <b>it's funny</b>. Much more consistently comical than the books, but with the same style of humour - i.e. lots of Ron being a buffoon. <br /><blockquote>
  <i><b>Hermione:</b> If some part of Voldemort survived, in whatever form, we need to be prepared. And I’m scared.<br /><b>Ginny:</b> I’m scared too.<br /><b>Ron:</b> Nothing scares me. Apart from Mum.</i>
</blockquote><br />The plot leaves a little something to be desired. Again, it feels different from the main series. It's not so much about the world and magic, but more about relationships, conflicts (particularly between Harry and Albus) and the dialogue between characters. I suppose this makes more sense in a play, where the story unravels through dialogue and not through an omniscient narrator.<br /><br />And, as I touched upon earlier, it feels... older. I don't know how well kids will appreciate the jokes about growing old and how Ron now says "oof" every time he sits down. Or the family drama between Harry and his son, Albus. But I liked it. <br /><br />I'm happy with this addition. I truly am. If it had been too similar to the seven novels, I feel it would have risked reopening a series that had been closed in a great place. Instead, we have something very unique and, for me, very entertaining. Some of the staging directions also leave me excited about seeing the play (when I win the lottery or acquire a magic wand, maybe).<br /><br />One thing I have to say that I said in another comment thread: <b>NOW, it's time to stop</b>. This was a risky experiment and it turned out to be fun, but JKR needs to leave this world alone now. I really do not want to read about old-age Harry, Ron and Hermione rolling around in magical wheelchairs. So, just stop.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14644597201653711675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1544306864" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1544306864" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1544306864?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1544306864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7670485095067182931">It was alright. It was just alright.<br/><br/>I know I gave this 4 stars, but to be honest, J.K. Rowling can write a dictionary with Harry Potter illustrations and I'd probably give it 4 stars, so my rating is almost irrelevant here, given my extreme bias.<br/><br/>The thing is, it was cute, it was sweet, it was entirely nostalgic to see the old crew again, but I hated the play format. As a person who grew up with Harry Potter, and who is in her early 30s now, I feel like I grew up with Harry Potter and the crew, a</span>
  <span id="freeText7670485095067182931" style="display:none">It was alright. It was just alright.<br><br>I know I gave this 4 stars, but to be honest, J.K. Rowling can write a dictionary with Harry Potter illustrations and I'd probably give it 4 stars, so my rating is almost irrelevant here, given my extreme bias.<br><br>The thing is, it was cute, it was sweet, it was entirely nostalgic to see the old crew again, but I hated the play format. As a person who grew up with Harry Potter, and who is in her early 30s now, I feel like I grew up with Harry Potter and the crew, and with the advent of this book, I have, in fact, grown old with them. It was lovely to see them again. It was like meeting old friends.<br><br>I don't feel old. I'm a more responsible person, for sure, but I feel young at heart. When we're young, adulthood, responsibilities, just the prospect of <i>adulting</i> seem so daunting...then one gets there and it's like, well, I'm as immature as I ever was. I love fun as much as I ever did. Growing old isn't that bad. And seeing the old crew being as much as they ever were brings joy into my not-yet-old-and-grizzled-heart.<br><br>I could do without the kids, to be honest. Oh, sure, they're little Potter and Granger-Weasley spawns, but come on, nobody ever has and nobody ever will win me over as much as their parents, whom I have loved the instant we met them on the Hogwarts Express.<br><br>(Ok, maybe not Ron...)<br><br>But I digress. The kids aren't all bad. I rather like little Scorpius, actually.<blockquote>
  <i>SCORPIUS: And it’s just like my father’s! I got his nose, his hair, and his name. Not that that’s a great thing either. I mean — father-son issues, I have them. But, on the whole, I’d rather be a Malfoy than, you know, the son of the Dark Lord.</i>
</blockquote>The adults have grown, they've changed. Some have changed so much that I hardly recognize them, Draco, for instance. I like that he's, well, <i>nicer</i> now, but he doesn't feel like Draco, you know? I've been so used to Harry and Draco doing this...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470066560ra/19885024.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That it's rather discombobulating to see anything otherwise.<br><br>But yeah, characters are great, but the format. THE FORMAT. <br><br>I don't even know it's fair of me to judge this based on the fact that I don't like that it's a play, because <b>for fuck's sakes, IT'S A PLAY</b>. Like, what did I expect? This may be the most confusing review I've ever written. I just don't like the play format. It's meant for the stage. That means it's up to the skill of the actors to portray what is implied. It's up to the audience to interpret nuances. It is almost entirely based on dialogue, and I hate that. I miss Rowling's writing. I love Rowling's writing, and I wanted more of it. The play brings up so many things that could have been written so much more, had it been expanded into a book format. The children's growing pains, particular that of young Albus. Harry's feelings as a parent. Draco's struggles with who he was and who he is. Furthermore, Ron is relegated to <b>little more than comic relief.</b> Let's be honest, I never liked the guy, but for him to be much of the same character that he ever was conjures up the image of the try-hard middle-aged dude, and I know that Ron is more than that.<br><br>I like it? I don't like it? I don't know. But I would certainly relish watching it on the stage if I ever had the chance. It's bound to be better than on paper.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7670485095067182931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1543987448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4088527506630227099">You know, I really hadn’t foreseen the publication of something to lengthen Harry Potter’s story after the conclusion that was <em>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows. </em><br/><br/>So, the way I see it, <em>Harry Potter and the Cursed Child </em>is a lovely gift to every Harry Potter fan out there who has hoped and waited a long time to see their wizard friends again.<br/><br/>Though the plot holes are very visible and spread throughout the story, they make for charming and heartfelt conversations between characters, so I didn’t </span>
  <span id="freeText4088527506630227099" style="display:none">You know, I really hadn’t foreseen the publication of something to lengthen Harry Potter’s story after the conclusion that was <em>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows. </em><br /><br />So, the way I see it, <em>Harry Potter and the Cursed Child </em>is a lovely gift to every Harry Potter fan out there who has hoped and waited a long time to see their wizard friends again.<br /><br />Though the plot holes are very visible and spread throughout the story, they make for charming and heartfelt conversations between characters, so I didn’t mind them all that much.<br /><br />The best thing about this #8 Harry Potter is how nostalgic it makes the reader feel. There are plenty of familiar faces – Harry, Ginny, Draco, Hermione, Ron, Dumbledore, etc – as well as some interesting new ones – Albus, Rose, Scorpius, Lily, James…<br /><br />Admittedly, it was strange to read this supposedly 8th story in Harry Potter’s world in play format but the truth is, it was extremely easy to imagine everything play out like in a movie, so it all felt alive to me.<br /><br />This isn’t a book you <em>have </em>to read but, if you’re a diehard Harry Potter fan, I am going to look at you quite incredulously if you decide not to. I’m sadly not going to be able to tell you that you're making the right choice, because this is so, so charming and fun, but I can understand people wanting to have their own vision of the Harry Potter cast as adults and their children. Yes, it's a bit silly but… I loved it still.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4088527506630227099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Reading this really felt like Harry Potter fan-fiction to me, partly because it's hard to wrap my head around an 8th (sort of) Harry Potter story and partly because reading it as a play instead of a novel just made it feel...less like Harry Potter. I didn't dislike it; I definitely didn't love it--but I do want to be fair and say that reading a play is never, <i>never</i> as good as seeing the live production. In theory maybe this book shouldn't exist because it won't ever do the story justice. However, I'm glad I got to read it because I don't think I'll ever get to London to see the real deal, and at least now I know what it's all about.</span>

<div id="review_1546021534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1546021534" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1546021534?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29058155-harry-potter-and-the-cursed-child">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=children-of-all-ages">children-of-all-ages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=1-star-reads">1-star-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1546021534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14044326756224662606">Now this was a real shame. It read like some juvenile fan fiction. The characters were utterly lifeless. Perhaps seeing this would be better. The stage actor’s performances would carry the emotion and drama the dialogue completely failed to convey.<br/><br/>The stage directions were also minimalistic. I mean we have a basic location set for us, but that’s about all. There’s no real expression or sense of urgency. All in all, it’s just a little flat. The plot is feasible, even if it felt a little forced, b</span>
  <span id="freeText14044326756224662606" style="display:none">Now this was a real shame. It read like some juvenile fan fiction. The characters were utterly lifeless. Perhaps seeing this would be better. The stage actor’s performances would carry the emotion and drama the dialogue completely failed to convey.<br /><br />The stage directions were also minimalistic. I mean we have a basic location set for us, but that’s about all. There’s no real expression or sense of urgency. All in all, it’s just a little flat. The plot is feasible, even if it felt a little forced, but the characters were just poor. The new ones aren’t so bad, but the old characters, Harry, Ron and Hermione, were barely themselves. They just had no depth to them; they’re like reflections of their surface level. Ron felt like a piece of furniture that seemed to enjoy inserting several badly times jokes. Hermione seemed cold. And Harry, Harry simply isn’t Harry. <br /><br />How can he identify himself as a bad farther? How can he believe that he had no farther figure in his own life? He had many. He had inspiration from many great men. They taught him a great deal about life and himself in the process. So why would a man who has defeated the face of evil be so daunted by giving his son some simple advice? It doesn’t add up. Harry Potter would make an excellent farther. <br /><br />This didn’t even feel like the same world.<br /><br />___________________________________<br /><br />You can connect with me on social media via <a href="https://linktr.ee/sean.ultra_vegan1" rel="nofollow noopener">My Linktree</a>.<br />__________________________________</span>
  <a data-text-id="14044326756224662606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1545866000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1545866000" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1545866000?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1545866000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2164466143936161474"><a href='https://bookspoils.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470027342ra/19880324.gif' width='500' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>This review contains <b>*mild spoilers*</b>.<br/><br/>I've waited for this particular story for what feels like ages, and words cannot even describe for how grateful I am that it finally exists in my hands. <b>Harry Potter and the Cursed Child</b> continues the wondrous magical world that we all know and love.<br/><br/>The story starts out at King's Cross with the original trio preparing their school-age children to board the train to start their first year at Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry.<br/><br/>It's at this time that</span>
  <span id="freeText2164466143936161474" style="display:none"><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470027342ra/19880324.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This review contains <b>*mild spoilers*</b>.<br><br>I've waited for this particular story for what feels like ages, and words cannot even describe for how grateful I am that it finally exists in my hands. <b>Harry Potter and the Cursed Child</b> continues the wondrous magical world that we all know and love.<br><br>The story starts out at King's Cross with the original trio preparing their school-age children to board the train to start their first year at Hogwarts School of Witchcraft and Wizardry.<br><br>It's at this time that Harry and his son, Albus, share a nice father-son moment:<br><br><i>“Albus: Dad . . .<br><br>Do you think — what if I am — what if I’m put in Slytherin . . .<br><br>Harry: And what would be wrong with that?<br><br>Albus: Slytherin is the House of the snake, of Dark Magic . . . It’s not a House of brave wizards.<br><br>Harry: Albus Severus, you were named after two headmasters of Hogwarts. One of them was a Slytherin and he was probably the bravest man I ever knew.”</i><br><br>(I dislike Snape, but the overall conversation made me tear up a bit.)<br><br>I also really appreciated that they talked about Slytherin in a positive light.<br><br>We have a few time jumps here and there, and then complications arise because Harry - Head of the Department of Magical Law Enforcement - seized an illegal Time-Turner from Theodore Nott and has kept it.<br><br><i>“The once-great Harry Potter, now a stone-cold Ministry man.”</i><br><br>Meanwhile, Albus gets sorted into Slytherin and struggles with the weight of a family legacy he never wanted.<br>Harry tries to reach out to Albus but finds that he has diffuclity understanding someone different. And their connection wobbles from year to year because of it.<br><br><i>“Harry: Do you want a hand? Packing. I always loved packing. It meant I was leaving Privet Drive and going back to Hogwarts. Which was . . . well, I know you don’t love it but . . .<br><br>Albus: For you, it’s the greatest place on earth. I know. The poor orphan, bullied by his uncle and aunt Dursley . . .<br><br>Harry: Albus, please — can we just —<br><br>Albus: . . . traumatized by his cousin, Dudley, saved by Hogwarts. I know it all, Dad. Blah, blah, blah.<br><br>Harry: I’m not going to rise to your bait, Albus Potter.<br><br>Albus: The poor orphan who went on to save us all. So may I say — on behalf of wizarding kind — how grateful we are for your heroism. Should we bow now or will a curtsy do?<br><br>Harry: Albus, please — you know, I’ve never wanted gratitude.<br><br>Albus: But right now I’m overflowing with it — it must be the kind gift of this moldy blanket that did it . . .<br><br>Harry: Moldy blanket?<br><br>Albus: What did you think would happen? We’d hug. I’d tell you I always loved you. What? What?<br><br>Harry (finally losing his temper): You know what? I’m done with being made responsible for your unhappiness. At least you’ve got a dad. Because I didn’t, okay?<br><br>Albus: And you think that was unlucky? I don’t.<br><br>Harry: You wish me dead?<br><br>Albus: No! I just wish you weren’t my dad.”</i><br><br>Harry and Albus are trying to reach each other here, both are failing.<br><br>As past and present fuse ominously, both father and son learn the uncomfortable truth: sometimes darkness comes from unexpected places.<br><br><b>The Cursed Child</b> answered a lot of topics that had been left unanswered in my mind, and it makes my heart tighten just thinking about everything.<br><br><i>“Harry: And I’ve locked away the map. You won’t see it again. Your mum left your room exactly as it was when you ran away — you know that? Wouldn’t let me go in — wouldn’t let anyone go in — you really scared her . . . And me.<br><br>Albus: Really scared you?<br><br>Harry: Yes.<br><br>Albus: I thought Harry Potter wasn’t afraid of anything?<br><br>Harry: Is that how I make you feel?<br><br>Albus looks at his dad, trying to figure him out.<br><br>ALBUS: I don’t think Scorpius said, but when we returned after failing to fix the first task, I was suddenly in Gryffindor House. Nothing was better between us then either — so — the fact that I’m in Slytherin — that’s not the reason for our problems. It’s not just about that.”</i><br><br>I really appreciated that their relationship was developed in a very honest and raw way.<br><br>And not only theirs, but the development of Draco and his son, Scorpius, was truly melting my everything.<br><br><i>“Draco: Astoria always knew that she was not destined for old age. She wanted me to have somebody when she left, because . . . it is exceptionally lonely, being Draco Malfoy. I never realized, though, that by hiding him away from this gossiping, judgmental world, I ensured that my son would emerge shrouded in worse suspicion than I ever endured.<br><br>Harry: Love blinds. We have both tried to give our sons, not what they needed, but what we needed. We’ve been so busy trying to rewrite our own pasts, we’ve blighted their present.”</i><br><br>Watching Draco care deeply and <b>fiercely</b> for his child made me open up my heart.<br><br>Oh, and I wanted to mention how ecstatic I was when Albus befriended a Malfoy. Their friendship was inspiring until the very last heartbreaking page.<br><br><i>“Scorpius: Your dad thinks the rumors are true — I am the son of Voldemort?<br><br>Albus (nods): His department are currently investigating it.<br><br>Scorpius: Good. Let them. Sometimes — sometimes I find myself thinking — maybe they’re true too.<br><br>Albus: No. They’re not true. And I’ll tell you why. Because I don’t think Voldemort is capable of having a kind son — and you’re kind, Scorpius. To the depths of your belly, to the tips of your fingers. I truly believe Voldemort — Voldemort couldn’t have a child like you.<br><br>Scorpius: That’s nice — that’s a nice thing to say.<br><br>Albus: And it’s something I should have said a long time ago. In fact, you’re probably the best person I know. And you don’t — you couldn’t — hold me back. You make me stronger — and when Dad forced us apart — without you —<br><br>Scorpius: I didn’t much like my life without you in it either."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470027342ra/19880325.gif" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We also had a lot of unexpected returns from the people that ended up sacrificing themselves in previous books, which truly broke me— I kept looking for Fred Weasley to show up and crack a joke... but, alas, you can't always get what you want.<br> <br>But to end this review on a more positive note, I want to mention my favorites: Hermione and Ron.<br> <br><i>“Ron: I mean, we’ve been together so long — and married for so long — I mean, so long —<br><br>Hermione: If this is your way of saying you want a marital break, Ron, then, to be clear, I will skewer you with this quill.<br><br>Ron: Shut up. Will you shut up for once? I want to do one of those marriage renewal things I’ve read about. Marriage renewal. What do you think?<br><br>Hermione (melting slightly): You want to marry me again?<br><br>Ron: Well, we were only young when we did it the first time and I got very drunk and — well, to be honest, I can’t remember much of it and . . . The truth is — I love you, Hermione Granger, and whatever time says — I’d like the opportunity to say so in front of lots of other people. Again. Sober.<br><br>She looks at him, she smiles, she pulls him to her, she kisses him.<br><br>Hermione: You’re sweet.<br><br>Ron: And you taste of toffee . . .”</i><br><br>I'm <b>always</b> up for more canon Romione.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470027343ra/19880326.gif" width="500" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To sum up, I thought at first that the format of the story would interfere with getting completely pulled in, but I needn't have worried— this book was the definition of unputdownable. It truly didn't take long for me to realize how much I missed reading about Harry Potter and his magical surroundings. Hogwarts will always be like home. And now... I'm getting tearful just thinking about what an impact it made on me, as both the reader and person I am today.<br><br>Also, it was pretty nice getting to know that both Harry Potter and I are afraid of pigeons:<br><br><i>“Harry: You told me you don’t think I’m scared of anything, and that — I mean, I’m scared of everything. I mean, I’m afraid of the dark, did you know that?<br><br>Albus: Harry Potter is afraid of the dark?<br><br>Harry: I don’t like small spaces and — I’ve never told anyone this, but I don’t much like — (he hesitates before saying it) pigeons.<br><br>Albus: You don’t like pigeons?<br><br>Harry (he scrunches up his face): Nasty, pecky, dirty things. They give me the creeps.”</i><br><br>Yes, Harry!!<br><br>Oh, and my favorite acts were acts 2 &amp; 4— because family dynamics and mystery!!<br>Just... I'm so glad this book exists, I truly missed my favorite trio.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470027343i/19880327.jpg" width="466" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470027343i/19880328.jpg" width="520" height="295" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>5/5 stars (of course)</b><br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>Harry Potter and the Cursed Child</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link. I'll make a small commission!*</i><br><a target="_blank" href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1338099132/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=9325&amp;creativeASIN=1338099132&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;tag=natalie013-20&amp;linkId=cc8a85cbf6db1f2515fcc62d79406196" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482928982i/21562518.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482928982i/21562519.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">This review and more can be found on my blog.</a></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22106879-jayson?shelf=format-script">format-script</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22106879-jayson?shelf=subject-boarding-school">subject-boarding-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736951116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6209908802557575140"><b>(B+) 79%</b> | Good<br/><i>Notes:</i> All the charm of the originals, but too steeped in revisiting previous storylines to be much more than good nostalgia.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1529064964" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1529064964" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1529064964?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29058155-harry-potter-and-the-cursed-child">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=what-the-hype">what-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=riddikulus">riddikulus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=convoluted-plans">convoluted-plans</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1529064964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7161372949064605840"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2016/08/review-harry-potter-and-the-cursed-child-by-j-k-rowling-jessicadhaluska.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>RULE FOR SPOILERS:</b> if it's in the first 10%, and therefore (in most cases) available for scrutiny from undecided readers in the FREE downloadable preview, <b>IT'S NOT A SPOILER.</b><br/><br/>That being said, a LOT of things happen--IMPORTANT things--in the first <em>five</em> percent, let alone ten percent of HARRY POTTER AND THE CURSED CHILD, so if you'd rather go into your read without significant prior knowledge, leave this review immediately.<br/><br/><b>That's the only warning you're going to get.</b><br/><br/>In my ex</span>
  <span id="freeText7161372949064605840" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2016/08/review-harry-potter-and-the-cursed-child-by-j-k-rowling-jessicadhaluska.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>RULE FOR SPOILERS:</b> if it's in the first 10%, and therefore (in most cases) available for scrutiny from undecided readers in the FREE downloadable preview, <b>IT'S NOT A SPOILER.</b><br><br>That being said, a LOT of things happen--IMPORTANT things--in the first <em>five</em> percent, let alone ten percent of HARRY POTTER AND THE CURSED CHILD, so if you'd rather go into your read without significant prior knowledge, leave this review immediately.<br><br><b>That's the only warning you're going to get.</b><br><br>In my experience there are two types of hardcore fans for any given series:<br><br><b>1. The Blind Zealot.</b><br><br>This type of fan will forgive an author almost anything. Inconsistent behavior in main characters, enormous plot holes, unexplained developments, etc., it doesn't matter, b/c OHMAGAWD, I LOVE IT SO MUCH!!! *squeeeeeeee*<br><br><b>2. The Thoughtful, Critical Reader.</b><br><br>This type of fan loves a series based solely on its merit. They aren't blind to the aforementioned plot holes or inconsistent characters, they are in fact disappointed by such occurrences, but they can still maintain LOVE for the overall series. <br><br>For example, I LOVE HARRY POTTER, but I did <em>not</em> love HARRY POTTER AND THE ORDER OF THE PHOENIX, b/c I felt Rowling encapsulated all the teenangsty emotions of adolescence a little bit too thoroughly. <br><br>It was, in a word, exhausting.<br><br><b>PLOT TWIST:</b> I think <em>both</em> types of fans are equally likely to have issues with this latest addition to their Harry Potter library.<br><br><b>Blind Zealots:</b><br><br>The trouble with ending a series is that if it's done well, you have all the answers to all of your questions, and a vague enough HEA-type scenario that your well-loved cast of characters is assured whatever it is that they deserve. <br><br>Heroines and Heroes live happily ever after, Villains and Minions are thwarted and punished, and while you aren't foolish enough to think everyone's adventures are over, Good continuing to triumph over Evil is reasonably guaranteed. <br><br>BUT.<br><br>Once you've finished something, the only way to reopen it is too create <em>new</em> conflict--without conflict there's no story. <br><br>Suddenly the nebulous "HEA" isn't so nebulous, and that new clarity jeopardizes everything you've happily assumed about <em>what comes next</em>.<br><br>Harry, Ginny, Hermione, and Ron, previously cardboard cutouts of adult wizards, become real parents with real children, and those children must grow up, making mistakes while they do it, and, <em>worse</em>, they must go through puberty and all the angst that entails.<br><br>That's not happily ever after . . . That's REAL LIFE. <br><br>Then Real Life takes your daydream of a-son-of-Harry-Potter being sorted into Slytherin and reinventing the house's image with the kind of unaffected rebelliousness you associated with a teenaged Sirius Black, and crushes it under its heel, forcing you to realize that wizards . . . are kind of assholes.<br><br>So now, adding insult to injury, the image of the utopian magical society that sprang fully formed from Voldemort's ashes is forever ruined.<br><br>A Blind Zealot might find ignorance preferable to that turn of events.<br><br>But those aren't my issues. My issues are thus:<br><br><b>1. I HATE TIME TRAVEL.</b><br><br>I've said it before, and I'll say it again: I'm an escapist reader. I need to be consumed by a book to fully enjoy it, and that means I NEED to be able to believe what I'm reading is the truth.<br><br>BUT.<br><br>Time travel destroys the possibility of believing anything, b/c it's ALL subject to change. <br><br>Why mourn a character's death if it will more than likely be nullified in the next chapter or two? Why dredge up any outrage on a character's behalf when the object of her torment will be thwarted during the second take?<br><br>For me, it's not an issue of, "why would I?" It's an issue of, "I can't." And if I can't feel anything in response to your characters or your story, why would I read your book?<br><br><b>2. Resurrecting Voldemort-as-villain is lazy. And infuriating.</b><br><br>We survived three of Voldemort's failed attempts at rebirth, we survived one success, and we survived a three book revelation that essentially said we had to kill him SEVEN TIMES for his death to actually stick.<br><br>After all of that, how could anyone think it would be a Good Idea to bring him back AGAIN?<br><br>Admittedly, it wasn't <i>quite </i>that simple, but . . . it was also exactly that simple. Everything and everyone else connected to ye olde grande scheme was superfluous, merely the means of achieving a so-very-tired end.<br><br>As for the aforementioned superfluous detail: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I recognize the futility of relying on Bellatrix LeStrange's marital status as an argument against her conceiving Voldemort's child. That crazy bitch was probably so euphoric at the idea of giving birth to her Master's spawn that she felt no pain during the actual delivery.<br><br>BUT.<br><br>No matter how much he wished it, Voldemort wasn't actually a god, so divine conception was an impossibility . . . Which means . . . He would have had to . . . Physically . . . Have . . . Sex . . . In order to produce offspring.<br><br>O______O<br><br>I don't think Bellatrix would've objected to the necessity--we've already established that she's a CRAZY BITCH.<br><br>BUT . . . I'm not convinced he was physically able:<br><br>A. At the alleged time of procreation, he was more snake than man. <br><br>B. Snakes don't have noses, neither did Voldemort.<br><br>C. Snakes don't have . . . do-NOT-make-me-say-it-you-know-where-this-is-going.<br><br>That's all I'm sayin'. *shrugs awkwardly*  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>3. Unnecessary drama.</b><br><br>At first I debated whether or not it was fair to fault a staged production for being overly dramatic, but I hate unnecessary drama on the screen as much as I hate it on paper, so, YES, it most definitely <em>is</em> fair.<br><br>A. Stop crying, dammit. Especially you, Harry. *rolls eyes*<br><br>B. Ginny's instant escalation from concerned-but-understanding wife into finger-pointing harridan. If you've read it, you know to what I'm referring.<br><br>C. Harry's impersonation of a father-as-dictator <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that I initially attributed to the first timeturning, but as he had his come-to-Jesus <i>before</i> the timeline was altered again, I'm forced to conclude was simply his epically poor parenting skills. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>4. Contradictions, including, but not limited to:</b><br><br>In Act 2, when Harry uses his conversation with Dumbledore-as-portrait as reasoning for his ludicrous request, Headmistress McGonagoll admonishes him for treating a "memoir" like the actual person:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>HARRY: And Dumbledore—Dumbledore said—<br>PROFESSOR McGONAGALL: What? <br>HARRY: His portrait. We spoke. He said some things which made sense—<br>PROFESSOR McGONAGALL: Dumbledore is dead, Harry. And I’ve told you before, portraits don’t represent even half of their subjects.</i>
</blockquote><br>BUT, in Act 4, this:<br><br><blockquote>DUMBLEDORE (<em>openly weeping now</em>): I was blind. That is what love does. I couldn’t see that you needed to hear that this closed-up, tricky, dangerous old man . . . loved you. <br><br><em>A pause. The two men are overcome with emotion.</em>
</blockquote><br>Either they're two men or they're one man and a flawed copy. Pick one and stick with it, please.<br><br><b>5. Plot holes.</b><br><br>A. If Dolores Umbrage warded her Hogwarts office against unauthorized entry, do you really expect me to believe that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Hermione wouldn't similarly ward the office of the MINISTER OF MAGIC? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>B. <i>How many times</i> have we heard some variation of, "Am I the only person who's read <i>Hogwarts, a History</i>?"<br><br>And how many of those times were specifically in reference to wards that prevented witches and wizards from magicking themselves onto Hogwarts' property? <br><br>Yet suddenly and inexplicably, anyone can use the floo network to travel to any number of chimneys on the grounds.<br><br>C. There was also some nonsense about Albus and Scorpius not needing to worry about a certain de-wanded Hogwarts student being harmed b/c "the professors would never allow serious injury to occur," which is, simply put . . . laughable.<br><br>That's not to say HARRY POTTER AND THE CURSED CHILD was horrible and I hated it. It wasn't and I didn't. I even loved parts of it, Scorpius in particular. BUT. Even taking into consideration that it was a script, not a novel, it wasn't the same level of quality we've come to expect from Rowling (who, no, may not have written the thing in its entirety, but who, YES, did collaborate on and ultimately give her seal of approval for), and that is disappointing. <br><br>I'm not going to bother recommending or not recommending this one--you'll either read it or you won't, and at this stage of series worship or indifference, your decision will have little to do with what I have to say about it. SO. Go forth and do what you were always going to do.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="7161372949064605840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText10932999212013243064" style="display:none">It's finally HERE!!! HP FOR LIFE!!<br><br>My post on <a href="http://hellobeautifulbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Hello Beautiful Book Blog</a><br><br>WHO'S EXCITED?!?<br>OMGGGGGGG<br>It's going to be published on HARRY'S BIRTHDAY!!!! <br>OH HAPPY DAYYYY<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455117477ra/18058631.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_o0d8loWWsn1sgl0ajo1_500_zps9pu5oos3.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455117477ra/18058632.gif" alt=" photo jk-rowling-posted-a-new-harry-potter-story-about-harry-potter_zpsfbhtyxxz.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455117477ra/18058633.gif" alt=" photo anigif_enhanced-buzz-12118-1387505440-9_zps8fmzwups.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455117477ra/18058634.gif" alt=" photo anigif_enhanced-buzz-20007-1399060810-32_zps7zgoutlk.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>FROM TIME MAGAZINE ONLINE:<br><blockquote>
  <i>"There’s good news for Harry Potter fans who won’t be able to make it to London to see the theatrical production of Harry Potter and the Cursed Child: the play will be published in book form immediately after its debut.<br><br>The script, written by Jack Thorne and based on a story by J.K. Rowling, Thorne and John Tiffany, will be published as an eBook by Pottermore, Rowling’s digital publishing platform, and in hardcover by Scholastic in the U.S. The first printing will be a “Special Rehearsal Edition,” reflecting the script from the early part of the preview period, and a later “Definitive Collector’s Edition” will present the finalized version (as many plays make small changes during previews).<br><br>The story picks up 19 years after the end of the original series, with Potter working at the Ministry of Magic, now a father of three. As Pottermore describes, “While Harry grapples with a past that refuses to stay where it belongs, his youngest son Albus must struggle with the weight of a family legacy he never wanted.”<br><br>The play premieres on July 30, and the book will be released July 31, which just so happens to be The Chosen One’s birthday."</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455120763i/18059226.jpg" alt=" photo fandom-harry-potter-Favim.com-754200_zpsdfgeuhin.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1543867966">

  <span id="freeText12164819038061470275" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>CONGRATS TO HARRY POTTER AND THE CURSED CHILD FOR WINNING THE 2016 GOODREADS CHOICE AWARDS FOR BEST FANTASY!!!</u>
</b><br><br><b>Bloody Hell!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470191859ra/19899419.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I freaking cried. I was afraid I wasn't going to like this book but I did and I damn cried. This is a SPOILER FREE review so I can't tell you what made me cry. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452801867ra/17745804.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though this is about the kids and all of our loves are older, they wrote the book in a way that we get to have some memories of certain things. And my favorite character made me cry again! <br><br>I really hope they put this play out on dvd sometime and make it available to everyone. Although, it might be weird seeing other people playing the parts. <br><br>Anyway, I loved reading about the children. I loved the friendship between Albus, Harry's son and Scorpius, Draco's son. Scorpius was the sweetest one of all, who would have thunk. <br><br>I didn't like some of the parts Ron played, he seemed like an idiot but he's Ron and I love Ron. <br><br>Of course most of you already know it's written in a play format. This was weird at first and then I got into it. I don't think I have ever read a play before, it seems like I would remember. <br><br>This was a nice little trip down Hogwarts Lane and the little mystery/hijinks the kids get up to that brings on all kinds of issues was a cool edition. Well, not really, but you know what I mean. <br><br>I loved it. I can't say that I loved everything about it and I might not have loved it if that one part didn't come into play, but who cares. I am so happy with it for what it is. I hope you all love it as much as I did and if you don't then that's okay too. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455396372ra/18097715.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>Thank you for being my light in the darkness</i>
</b><br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/08/harry-potter-and-cursed-child-by-jk.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

  <b>DRACO: </b>
  <i>I don’t care what you did or who you saved, you are a constant curse on my family, Harry Potter.</i>
</blockquote><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470142372i/19893683._SY540_.png' width='450' height='420' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>A 'Play', of friendship, courage & anti-prejudice as before..<br/>AND<br/>Marital relations, Father/Son issues.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470493974ra/19935015.gif' width='450' height='259' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>A new Story goes farther than ever..<br/>travelling back & forth in time..<br/>Then back to where it all began..<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470145280ra/19894194.gif' width='450' height='266' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>To close the circle.<br/>Once & for all.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470157377i/19895811._SX540_.jpg' width='450' height='328' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469980161i/19877051._SX540_.jpg' width='450' height='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><blockquote>
  <b>HARRY: </b>
  <i>The Boy Who Lived. How many people have</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6949947264095961209" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470761587i/19962312._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="276" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>They're back..One More time..19 years later.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455125330ra/18059923.gif" width="450" height="450" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>In a different style..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455125330ra/18059924.gif" width="450" height="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Harry Potter &amp; The Cursed 8th Book</b><blockquote>
  <b>DRACO: </b>
  <i>I don’t care what you did or who you saved, you are a constant curse on my family, Harry Potter.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470142372i/19893683._SY540_.png" width="450" height="420" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>A 'Play', of friendship, courage &amp; anti-prejudice as before..<br>AND<br>Marital relations, Father/Son issues.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470493974ra/19935015.gif" width="450" height="259" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>A new Story goes farther than ever..<br>travelling back &amp; forth in time..<br>Then back to where it all began..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470145280ra/19894194.gif" width="450" height="266" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>To close the circle.<br>Once &amp; for all.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470157377i/19895811._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="328" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469980161i/19877051._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>HARRY: </b>
  <i>The Boy Who Lived. How many people have to die for the Boy Who Lived?</i>
</blockquote><b><br>A Bittersweet ending to The Saga of The Boy Who Lived.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455125495ra/18059937.gif" width="450" height="192" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Our</i> Friends are different a little bit here than we knew them?<br><i>YES</i>, I mean who isn't? It's 19 years later.. Are you now as you'd expected would be 10 years ago? Are your real life friends still the same 12, 15 years later?<br><br></b>The Story is in Different form &amp; atmosphere?<br><b> YES.</b>, It's a Play..screen play - and not to mention that there's a <b>‘Definitive Edition’ </b>of the play as it is just <i>the Rehearsal Edition</i>.. <br><br>Not the Trio story rather the children's?<b> YES.</b> It's story of 19 years later...of the new generation..<br>So STOP <i>Moaning like Myrtle</i>,It's still very faithful to the magical series..<br><br>A perfect conclusion to the Symmetry* of the Epic series in the History.<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~<br><br>Since the Ending of <b>Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows</b> we wanted more...One more time.<br>Many asking too many "What If"..<br><i>What if Harry's son end up in Slytherin?<br>What if Ron and Hermione didn't work out as the author herself suspects?<br>What if there's a Time Turner left?<br>What if we use it to save someone of Death?<br>What if we use it to save Voldemort? or to make more Horcrux ? Or worst? <br><b>What if we had One More Book? Nineteenth Years Later?</b></i><br><br><u>**The Play**</u><br>--------<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470764329i/19962630._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="292" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>First of all, Please do a Worldwide tour...Please include Egypt.<br>It's easy to read, and to get into the story..<br>Alas, I have to admit that being in form of ‘play’ and not a novel made it even a bit “dry” like most Fan Fictions.,<i> I even thought, after spending a direct 6 hours reading 3 Acts that it may be one and not the real deal -since I read it first in ebook format till my hard copy arrive to Egypt- </i><br><br>Anyway, You have to use your imagination to get the scenes...recall your past experience, life in Hogwarts and you'll be easily in...<b>Reliving the Magic</b><br><br>Add to being a play, it's not all by J.K. Rowling, the story is by her, Jack Thorne and John Tiffany together..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455127839i/18060234.jpg" width="400" height="253" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And the Playwright is by Jack Thorne...not Rowling.<br><b><br>Yet the lines are really fun, smart..just amazing.<br>And you have to let go once you start ‘Act Two’ cause everything starts to heat up much..in a very fast packed adventure, and theatrical dramatic ones…<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470181319i/19898527._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="253" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Story<br>--------<br>“Can you Keep the Secret?”</b><br><i>Will try my best.</i><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<b><br>It's different... more mature...real wild and dangerous cause it deals with the most dangerous Instruments...TIME..<br>This time you'd feel that Rowling is really cruel to the characters..<br>It may be about the Test of Life....To Choose between what's good and what's easy..<br>BUT it was real hard test to us all..</b><br><br>I will merely summing up only Act One..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470181319i/19898528._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="253" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It starts right with the “Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows” Epilogue scene..<br>Albus Severus Potter is worried sick he'd end up in Slythrine<br>Yet.. as soon as he started his year, this was the least of his troubles.<br>Surprisingly befriended with Scorpius Malfoy, surprisingly hates Hogwarts…<br>Surprisingly hates being the child of The Boy Who Lived, while many died in his cause.<br>The Father/Son issue in its worst..<br><br>And before his fourth year starts..Everything happens fast…<br>Harry as Ministry official and Hermione as Minister for Magic seize an illegal last Time Turner..that even more dangerous..<br>Amos Diggory wants his son back...who had been killed by Voldmort in the Triwizard Tournament more than 20 years ago..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470232101i/19904355.jpg" width="450" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Albus feels his father's responsible for this death..<br>An attempt to change a minor misfortune of the past leads into a massive , colossal damage to the present and the future..<br>And even turns into a horrible Dystopia.<br><b><br>It's like The Butterfly Effect… Days of Future Past<br><br>Again it's a story of the value of Friendship… The wrong of Prejudice... <br>But it's also about Father/Son relation very well written..<br></b>I loved how it goes, from wrong to kinda right.<br>Between Harry and Albus, Between Dumbledore and Harry…<br>And even between Draco and Scorpius..<br><b>Also the Marital relation is really good here…<br></b>I loved Ron and Hermione their opposite character yet their strong bond.<br>And the love that lived...between Harry and Ginny.<br>Oh and Draco and his wife…<br>Okay, time for,<br><b><br>The Characters<br>-----------<br>Again... Rowling is really cruel to her characters here..<br>Harry's being a "Hot Head" is clearly deepening the problem with his son.. <br></b>he's always has been a hot head by the way..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465749853i/19396445._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="253" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>yet Ginny is a good mother, and better wife than I expected.<br><br>Hermone was good , not excellent but I LOVED how she turned into two different characters .. one was really awesome in the Dystopia, the second was really bad...but that may match what happened.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470130967i/19890913._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="231" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I just may be didn't like Ron much that I didn't feel angry enough for him being a bit shallow in this play but that still a bit sad.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470231992i/19904329._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="253" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And I have to admit that I really LOVE how Draco is...with his still being have the trace of what he was before...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470130967i/19890914._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="253" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>BUT don't forget it's not about Harry Potter anymore...it's more about the Kids...<br>Though I wished to see more of Rose who's been shallow but I just loved Albus and Scorpios..<br><br>You'll be surprised with who you're gonna meet here.. truly.<br>Some of the Characters we all love makes appearance, some of them even you may never expect to see again!!!! <br><br>I have to say that I felt goosebumps everytime an old character appears...not just flashbacks, some was in The Future Past, or a real dystopia, some in dreams, even in portraits and some are just mentioned.<br><br>I really loved it. And wished for even more.<br>I was so sad for the death of some, and the re-death of some..<br><br>And just remember ... when you're 40.. you don't live the adventures much as your children..<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470231992i/19904330._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="252" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And this last story is about them after all....<br>The Children..<br><br><b><br>Who's The Cursed Child<br>-------------------</b><br><i>As if I'm gonna tell, ha!</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470231992i/19904331._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="223" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Till the mid of the third act you'll have many suspicious.<br><br>In Harry Potter’s dreams here he can be The Cursed Child...<br><i>-one of the best haunting scenes in every early novels was always Harry’s dreams, I bet it's purely written by Rowling here-</i><br>oh and looking from The Dursleys perspective, he is..even worse, he's so in his Son's eyes as well…<br>And that's what triggers everything here.<br>Many surprises, many twists…<br>I loved it… I loved the ending as well…<br><br>Playing in time is dangerous and as every one since the last book asked about <b>Why Not Using the Time Turner</b>….here's the answer..in the last book of the Series that changed the History forever..<br><br><b>Letting Go.<br>------------<br>By the end of this book you'll realize why J.K. Rowling announced that that's it for Harry Potter stories… it is the the full circle… the Beginning meets the End..the time has answered every What-if we can think of.<br><br>What if we use the time Turner to...<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470145280ra/19894194.gif" width="450" height="266" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It's all here.<br><br>19 Years for most of us, since the release of Harry Potter and the Philosopher’s Stone in 1997...Reading the story of Harry and his friends in 7 Volumes..<br>Reading as many lines about the back story of them and the rest of characters in the Pottermore and social media by Rowling. <br>Craving for one more time with them...after the Epilogue that passed 19 years.</b><i><br>Get excited with the very short article 2 years ago on Dumbledore Army reunited in the Qudditch World Cup.</i><br><br><b>Now here it is, a full story, one last story full of love and nostalgia.<br>We can't go back in time. We shan't dwell in the past..<br></b><br>And when I finish it, 2 times, I really admit <b>This is EVERYTHING I've ever wanted in a Harry Potter sequels </b><i>but I just wish a Time Turner, back to 1997 and start reading Harry Potter all over again.... :)</i><br><br>It's not good to dwell in past anyway, so I'm just Happy I lived this series..grown up with it..<br>I, and many of Potterheads and fans, were worried sick it may let us down but I'm so glad that many liked it.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470231992i/19904332._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="253" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And it's bittersweet to know that's it.<br><i>BUT We must have THE ‘Definitive Edition’ of the play that promised.</i><br><br>The series of Harry Potter, the boy who lived,is now complete…<br><br>And we still have a Wizarding World so vast to explore.<br>With J.K. Rowling, our Queen of Magic.<br><br>Mohammed Arabey<br>From 31 July 2016<br>To 1 Aug. 2016<br><i><br><br>**“ The Symmetry in case you didn't notice it yet.”<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470157377i/19895812._SY540_.jpg" width="448" height="688" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And you can really add more similarities to that .<br>This time it's so related to the Heart of the Series,<b>Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire </b>which is heavily echoes here..<br><br>If you agree about the symmetrical relation specially between this one and Goblet of Fire, let's discuss it at the comments :)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6949947264095961209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I went into this being apprehensive. My expectations were low and I was right. I just felt like Harry Potter's story ended where it had to end.   <span id="freeText2377882104115237948" style="display:none">SPOILER FREE VIDEO REVIEW: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/WUFTFkyDHlY">https://youtu.be/WUFTFkyDHlY</a><br /><br />2.5* (I think)<br />So here's the deal. I went into this being apprehensive. My expectations were low and I was right. I just felt like Harry Potter's story ended where it had to end. The questions that were left unanswered kept the story alive as I would imagine what might be going on in their lives as adults. This answers all those questions and then some. I wanted to rate this higher but I think 2.5 is as high as I can go. These characters didn't feel like the characters I fell in love with. The story had cringe worthy moments and honestly felt like fan fiction. I think seeing this actually performed would be incredible, but reading it was just, average. Might do a video review so I can go more into depth because I definitely have more to say.</span>
